# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Envoy Extension Registry and Factory Architecture

## Your Task

Perfect! I've created a comprehensive JSON file at `/workspace/answer.json` containing all the C++ source files and patterns that implement Envoy's extension registry system.

## Summary

The Envoy extension registry pattern is built around three core template classes in `envoy/registry/registry.h`:

1. **FactoryRegistry<Base>** - Static template class maintaining a registry of factories for a base type
2. **RegisterFactory<T, Base>** - Template class that self-registers extensions at static initialization time  
3. **FactoryCategoryRegistry** - Groups factories by category for discovery

**Key findings:**

- **Self-registration mechanism**: Extensions use `REGISTER_FACTORY` and `LEGACY_REGISTER_FACTORY` macros to create static instances that automatically register themselves during program startup (e.g., in `source/extensions/filters/http/wasm/config.cc`, `source/extensions/access_loggers/fluentd/config.cc`)

- **Base factory interfaces**: All factories inherit from `UntypedFactory` or `TypedFactory` defined in `envoy/config/typed_config.h`, providing name, category, and configuration type information

- **Factory lookup**: The `source/common/config/utility.h` provides lookup functions (`getFactory`, `getAndCheckFactory`) that retrieve registered factories by name or configuration type

- **52 relevant C++ files** including core registry implementation, test helpers, base factory classes, factory implementations, and utility functions

The complete findings with file paths, symbols, function chain, and detailed narrative explanation are in the JSON file.

\"Utility::getAndCheckFactory\"\n    }\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"The Envoy extension registry system is implemented through a template-based C++ design pattern that enables dynamic discovery and instantiation of extensions. Here is the comprehensive architecture:\\n\\n## Core Registry Pattern\\n\\nThe main registry implementation is in `envoy/registry/registry.h`, which contains three key template classes:\\n\\n1. **FactoryRegistry<Base>**: A static template class that maintains a registry of factories for a given base factory type. It implements:\\n   - `factories()`: Returns the static map of registered factories\\n   - `registerFactory()`: Registers a factory instance with a given name\\n   - `getFactory()`: Retrieves a factory by name\\n   - `registeredNames()`: Lists all registered factory names\\n   - `versionedFactories()`: Stores vendor-specific version information\\n   - `factoriesByType()`: Maps configuration message types to factories\\n   - `disableFactory()`: Disables a factory by name\\n\\n2. **RegisterFactory<T, Base>**: A template class used to register a factory at static initialization time. Its constructor automatically registers an instance of template parameter T with the FactoryRegistry<Base>. When instantiated statically, it causes the factory to self-register during program startup.\\n\\n3. **FactoryCategoryRegistry**: A static registry that groups factories by category (e.g., \\\"envoy.filters.listener\\\", \\\"envoy.access_logs\\\"), enabling discovery of all factories within a category.\\n\\n## Static Extension Registration\\n\\nExtensions self-register at static initialization time using two macros defined in `envoy/registry/registry.h`:\\n\\n- **REGISTER_FACTORY(FactoryClass, BaseFactoryClass)**: Creates a static instance of RegisterFactory<FactoryClass, BaseFactoryClass>, causing automatic registration during program initialization.\\n- **LEGACY_REGISTER_FACTORY(FactoryClass, BaseFactoryClass, DeprecatedName)**: Registers a factory with deprecated name support for backwards compatibility.\\n\\nThese macros are used throughout the codebase in config.cc files (e.g., `source/extensions/filters/http/wasm/config.cc`, `source/extensions/access_loggers/fluentd/config.cc`), where each extension implementation creates a static factory registration.\\n\\n## Base Factory Architecture\\n\\nAll extensions inherit from factory base classes defined in `envoy/config/typed_config.h`:\\n\\n- **UntypedFactory**: Base class requiring `name()`, `category()`, and optional `configTypes()` methods.\\n- **TypedFactory**: Extends UntypedFactory, requiring `createEmptyConfigProto()` to support type-safe configuration validation.\\n\\nSpecialized factory base classes for different extension types include:\\n- `ClusterFactory` in `envoy/upstream/cluster_factory.h`\\n- `NamedListenerFilterConfigFactory`, `NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory` in `envoy/server/filter_config.h`\\n- `AccessLogInstanceFactory` in `envoy/access_log/access_log_config.h`\\n- `TracerFactory` in `envoy/server/tracer_config.h`\\n- `TypedMetadataFactory` in `envoy/config/typed_metadata.h`\\n\\n## Factory Instantiation and Lookup\\n\\nThe `source/common/config/utility.h` file provides utility functions for factory discovery:\\n\\n- `Utility::getFactoryByName<Factory>(name)`: Looks up a factory by name, returns nullptr if not found\\n- `Utility::getAndCheckFactoryByName<Factory>(name)`: Looks up by name with error checking\\n- `Utility::getFactory<Factory, ProtoMessage>(message)`: Looks up by type URL or name\\n- `Utility::getAndCheckFactory<Factory, ProtoMessage>(message)`: Type-safe factory lookup with validation\\n\\nThese functions internally call `Registry::FactoryRegistry<Factory>::getFactory(name)` to retrieve the registered factory instance.\\n\\n## Template Factory Bases\\n\\nCommon extension patterns use template base classes for consistent implementation:\\n- `source/extensions/tracers/common/factory_base.h`: FactoryBase<ConfigProto> template for tracer factories\\n- `source/extensions/compression/common/compressor/factory_base.h`: CompressorLibraryFactoryBase template\\n- `source/extensions/filters/network/thrift_proxy/filters/factory_base.h`: FactoryBase<ConfigProto> for Thrift filters\\n- `source/extensions/filters/network/dubbo_proxy/filters/factory_base.h`: FactoryBase<ConfigProto> for Dubbo filters\\n\\n## Test Infrastructure\\n\\nTest utilities in `test/test_common/registry.h` provide:\\n- **InjectFactory<Base>**: Test helper that injects a mock factory and restores the original on destruction\\n- **InjectFactoryCategory<Base>**: Test helper for registering factory categories in tests\\n\\nThe test file `test/common/config/registry_test.cc` demonstrates:\\n- Registration of test factories using REGISTER_FACTORY\\n- Verification that factories are discoverable by name and category\\n- Support for versioned factories with version metadata\\n- Proper isolation and restoration of factory registrations in tests\\n\\n## Extension Discovery and Validation\\n\\nThe file `test/exe/check_extensions_against_registry_test.cc` shows how the system discovers all registered extensions through `FactoryCategoryRegistry::registeredFactories()` and validates that extension configuration types match those declared in the registry.\\n\\nThis design achieves loose coupling between Envoy core and extensions, allowing extensions to be compiled into the binary and discovered at runtime through the registry, with support for versioning, deprecation, and type-safe configuration.\"\n}\n",

instantiation of extensions. Here is the comprehensive architecture:\\n\\n## Core Registry Pattern\\n\\nThe main registry implementation is in `envoy/registry/registry.h`, which contains three key template classes:\\n\\n1. **FactoryRegistry<Base>**: A static template class that maintains a registry of factories for a given base factory type. It implements:\\n   - `factories()`: Returns the static map of registered factories\\n   - `registerFactory()`: Registers a factory instance with a given name\\n   - `getFactory()`: Retrieves a factory by name\\n   - `registeredNames()`: Lists all registered factory names\\n   - `versionedFactories()`: Stores vendor-specific version information\\n   - `factoriesByType()`: Maps configuration message types to factories\\n   - `disableFactory()`: Disables a factory by name\\n\\n2. **RegisterFactory<T, Base>**: A template class used to register a factory at static initialization time. Its constructor automatically registers an instance of template parameter T with the FactoryRegistry<Base>. When instantiated statically, it causes the factory to self-register during program startup.\\n\\n3. **FactoryCategoryRegistry**: A static registry that groups factories by category (e.g., \\\"envoy.filters.listener\\\", \\\"envoy.access_logs\\\"), enabling discovery of all factories within a category.\\n\\n## Static Extension Registration\\n\\nExtensions self-register at static initialization time using two macros defined in `envoy/registry/registry.h`:\\n\\n- **REGISTER_FACTORY(FactoryClass, BaseFactoryClass)**: Creates a static instance of RegisterFactory<FactoryClass, BaseFactoryClass>, causing automatic registration during program initialization.\\n- **LEGACY_REGISTER_FACTORY(FactoryClass, BaseFactoryClass, DeprecatedName)**: Registers a factory with deprecated name support for backwards compatibility.\\n\\nThese macros are used throughout the codebase in config.cc files (e.g., `source/extensions/filters/http/wasm/config.cc`, `source/extensions/access_loggers/fluentd/config.cc`), where each extension implementation creates a static factory registration.\\n\\n## Base Factory Architecture\\n\\nAll extensions inherit from factory base classes defined in `envoy/config/typed_config.h`:\\n\\n- **UntypedFactory**: Base class requiring `name()`, `category()`, and optional `configTypes()` methods.\\n- **TypedFactory**: Extends UntypedFactory, requiring `createEmptyConfigProto()` to support type-safe configuration validation.\\n\\nSpecialized factory base classes for different extension types include:\\n- `ClusterFactory` in `envoy/upstream/cluster_factory.h`\\n- `NamedListenerFilterConfigFactory`, `NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory` in `envoy/server/filter_config.h`\\n- `AccessLogInstanceFactory` in `envoy/access_log/access_log_config.h`\\n- `TracerFactory` in `envoy/server/tracer_config.h`\\n- `TypedMetadataFactory` in `envoy/config/typed_metadata.h`\\n\\n## Factory Instantiation and Lookup\\n\\nThe `source/common/config/utility.h` file provides utility functions for factory discovery:\\n\\n- `Utility::getFactoryByName<Factory>(name)`: Looks up a factory by name, returns nullptr if not found\\n- `Utility::getAndCheckFactoryByName<Factory>(name)`: Looks up by name with error checking\\n- `Utility::getFactory<Factory, ProtoMessage>(message)`: Looks up by type URL or name\\n- `Utility::getAndCheckFactory<Factory, ProtoMessage>(message)`: Type-safe factory lookup with validation\\n\\nThese functions internally call `Registry::FactoryRegistry<Factory>::getFactory(name)` to retrieve the registered factory instance.\\n\\n## Template Factory Bases\\n\\nCommon extension patterns use template base classes for consistent implementation:\\n- `source/extensions/tracers/common/factory_base.h`: FactoryBase<ConfigProto> template for tracer factories\\n- `source/extensions/compression/common/compressor/factory_base.h`: CompressorLibraryFactoryBase template\\n- `source/extensions/filters/network/thrift_proxy/filters/factory_base.h`: FactoryBase<ConfigProto> for Thrift filters\\n- `source/extensions/filters/network/dubbo_proxy/filters/factory_base.h`: FactoryBase<ConfigProto> for Dubbo filters\\n\\n## Test Infrastructure\\n\\nTest utilities in `test/test_common/registry.h` provide:\\n- **InjectFactory<Base>**: Test helper that injects a mock factory and restores the original on destruction\\n- **InjectFactoryCategory<Base>**: Test helper for registering factory categories in tests\\n\\nThe test file `test/common/config/registry_test.cc` demonstrates:\\n- Registration of test factories using REGISTER_FACTORY\\n- Verification that factories are discoverable by name and category\\n- Support for versioned factories with version metadata\\n- Proper isolation and restoration of factory registrations in tests\\n\\n## Extension Discovery and Validation\\n\\nThe file `test/exe/check_extensions_against_registry_test.cc` shows how the system discovers all registered extensions through `FactoryCategoryRegistry::registeredFactories()` and validates that extension configuration types match those declared in the registry.\\n\\nThis design achieves loose coupling between Envoy core and extensions, allowing extensions to be compiled into the binary and discovered at runtime through the registry, with support for versioning, deprecation, and type-safe configuration.\"\n}\n",
